  118. First off, Sonicare makes the best toothbrushes around. I've been using Sonicares for years and they are simply the best toothbrushes available. The Sonicare ProResults brush heads are great, and a huge improvement over the old design. The old design tended to accumulate water, toothpaste residual, and saliva inside it, which would then crust and get nasty if you didn't clean it regularly. Cleaning it was also a pain because crap would get stuck up inside it and you'd need to fish it out with a q-tip or something. The Sonicare ProResults brush heads improve on the old design by having a simple joint to connect it to the toothbrush. No more crap building up inside the toothbrush. Sonicare recommends that change the toothbrush head every 3 months, but I usually push it to 4 or 5 months. A cleaning tip would be to always remove the toothbrush head from the toothbrush itself, rinse it with some water, then let it sit on a clean paper towel to dry.

Overall, these heads do a good job.<br /><br />My complaint is on the design of these heads and the toothbrush in general. These heads leave a gap between them and the handle of the toothbrush where toothpaste residue can easily accumulate. It isn't too much of a hassle to pull it off every week or so and clean, but it seems like the problem is a little bit deeper than that. This gap allows buildup to accumulate around the rubber diaphragm that surrounds the vibrating metal core. A few weeks ago when pulling the head off my toothbrush and cleaning the residue out, I noticed that this residue/bacteria has been infiltrating or absorbing into that rubber diaphragm. The rubber has odd nodules on it. So it appears that the rubber is not impervious to penetration by bacteria. It may only be a matter of time before the rubber breaks down due to this penetration.<br /><br />So, while the design of these heads and the toothbrush is nice, it does require continual removal and cleaning. This may prevent the above situation. The design of the e-Series, while bulkier, does not have this issue.<br /><br />Also, it is difficult to remember to change your heads so I put a reminder in my calendar if that helps. Otherwise the heads from the subscribe-and-save just pile up!<br /><br />Hope this review was helpful. If there are questions or if there is anything I can clarify, please leave me a comment.

  832. These are replacement brushes for the Phillips SoniCare HX6932/10 toothbrush I reviewed in 2010: http://www.amazon.com/review/R3QPW8DYK5RLN0/ref=cm_cr_rdp_perm . You find out AFTER you've ordered them, and the projected delivery date is 5-6 weeks away. To be fair, the vendor's Amazon storefront DOES says they are UK-based, but who orders from the storefront? Even weirder are vendors with \\"USA\\" in their name who ALSO ship from England. Feels a bit scammy. Anyway, it worked out fine, as they shipped quickly (free) and by airmail, and the brushes arrived on the 9th day following the order (including the Memorial Day weekend, not celebrated in England). I guess the projected delivery date assumes delivery via a slow boat to/from China!<br /><br />Bottom line: these brushes are perfect replacements for several models of the Sonicare line, at a slight discount (maybe 20%) off retail. I would reiterate another person's comment that you do NOT need to replace these every 3 months, as advised. The \\"wear indicator\\" is a scam, and shows need for replacement within a few weeks. These brush heads maintain their structural integrity for up to a YEAR, with twice-daily use. I change mine about every 6 months. But even at $8/each, they are well worth it if you save on really expensive periodontal procedures.
